Letter

To the Editor-in-Chief:

Having read the news item "Armed Water Police Flee" in the "Local News" column of your newspaper on the 26th of this month, there are some discrepancies with the facts. Here is a brief account of the case: Wang Zixun, a second-class patrol officer of the No. 2 patrol of the No. 4 squadron of the 17th team of the original garrisoned Hengsha Water Police, left his post without permission. Three water patrols, Yang Wenpu, Zhang Shujing, and Cao Fang'an, colluded with bandits and fled on the night of September 23, carrying firearms. After hearing the news, our district immediately issued orders to investigate and arrest them. Subsequently, Gong Mianqin, the captain of the 17th team, reported to us, and we have already submitted a report to the Provincial Department for their arrest. As for patrol officer Wang Zixun, he left his post beforehand and has avoided meeting since the incident. We have ordered a strict arrest, but there is still no news of his whereabouts. This is the true course of events. I am writing to request a correction to clarify the truth and hope that you will publish it in your newspaper's "Letters" column. I wish you peace.

From the Fourth District Department of the Jiangsu Water Police Corps, October 28th.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Hai Ke

Wife (sitting up in bed in the middle of the night): Dear! Do you hear that? There are thieves downstairs.

Husband: No, no. Go back to sleep.

Wife: Listen. I know there must be thieves downstairs.

Husband: I know there are definitely no thieves downstairs.

Wife: You're mistaken. There must be thieves downstairs.

Thief (from the back room, speaking): Madam, your husband is right. We are all upstairs.

A (watching the excitement at the entrance of a birthday celebrant's home): How old is that birthday mother, anyway? She looks very strong.

B: Didn't you see the golden characters on that birthday banner? It clearly says "Ninetieth Grand Celebration." That madam is already ninety years old.

A: What about that skinny old man standing next to her? Who is he?

B: That's her husband. He's eighty-eight years old this year.

A: But why is he looking so miserable and unhappy?

B: Because he's been paying the life insurance premiums for his wife for forty years and still has to keep paying. He's extremely resentful.

Female A: When you get married in the future, what kind of person do you plan to marry?

Female B: I want to marry a doctor. When I get sick, someone will be there to treat me, and I won't have to pay.

Female A: I think you'll die eventually. You might as well marry a coffin shop owner. When you die, you'll have a good coffin, and you won't have to pay.

Snippets from Overseas

— Lao Feng

Seven years have passed since I left the bustling city of Paris. When I think of my travels in the past, it's as if I'm tracing the inscriptions on ancient, mottled steles. It's so vague. Zhang Jiangling once said, "My mind travels through the nine border fortresses, two or three times a day." Every time I think of these words, I can't help but linger. My former classmates have returned home one after another, their carriages filling the capital, to serve the Party and the country. Only my friend, Mr. Chen, continues to move forward. Isn't he an extraordinary person? The moon is setting on the roof beams, and I miss his face. The friendship of an old friend is profound, and a letter has come all the way from overseas. I excerpt a few points to aid our conversation. I dare not use exciting or stimulating words to bother my readers.

Ten Diplomats Can't Catch Up with International Glory is Originally Meant for Diplomats to Catch Up. But if a country produces a world-famous filmmaker or athlete, it may win considerable prestige for the country. Or the gains may be several times greater than those of diplomats. If you don't believe me, look at the example of the Japan-U.S. competition. In a certain Japan-U.S. tennis match overseas, the competition was for the world's number one record. Naturally, it caused a sensation among the French public, who have always valued sports. During the match, the judge made a mistake and gave Japan one more point. The Japanese athlete immediately deliberately lost one point to show that he was very unwilling to accept a point obtained by luck. The crowd in the stands naturally unanimously praised the Japanese athlete's noble morality as unattainable. The next morning, the newspapers printed headlines to praise him. The conclusion also said that the glory won by an athlete in the international arena is something that ten diplomats cannot catch up with.

A French Old Lady Makes a Solemn Vow One day, a French lady came to my (Mr. Chen refers to himself) residence and asked for the address of a Chinese classmate. Her expression was very different from her usual friendly and approachable demeanor. I was very surprised. Taking the opportunity, I asked her what was going on. She angrily explained the details to me. I learned that this classmate had been living in her house for a long time. But he neither studied nor worked. He was busy socializing with friends of different races and genders, dancing, and enjoying big meals. He was having a great time. Sometimes, when the government funding didn't arrive and he was short of money, he would ask her to lend him a little money. As a result, he accumulated thousands of francs. Later, he left on some pretext. Even during the New Year and holidays, he still sent her a greeting card. But the addresses he wrote were all fake. She didn't understand his deceit and went to find him according to the address, but she was just chasing shadows. I was so ashamed when I heard this story. By chance, a few days later, another classmate wanted to find a house and went to her house. She resolutely said "Je n'ai rien à faire avec les Chinois" (meaning "I never want to associate with the Chinese"). This classmate was turned away, still baffled. This kind of thing doesn't amount to much in the country. But abroad, it's not an individual issue but a collective issue. So, when I'm overseas, I'm like walking on thin ice, always vigilant. Although it's difficult to hope that I can increase the glory of the nation alone, I dare not belittle myself and cause shame to the entire nation.

Paper Quilt

— Mo Chi

In a previous issue of Free Talk, it was mentioned that a certain gentleman had no quilt in winter and instead pasted thick newspaper together to make a covering. He would curl up inside it at night as a regular habit. People found it strange and pitied his circumstances. Little did they know that this was exactly what the ancients called a "paper quilt." When I read Zhang Xiaoxiang's Yuhu Collection, there are two poems sending paper quilts to Han Zhongfu. One of them says, "Han Lang's incense is exhausted, and all connections are severed. The tattered cassock is burned by the lamp for Buddhist incense. I beg to give him a paper quilt as warm as cotton, to stir up dreams in his drunkenness." The other says, "I know that all dreams are illusions, and illusions often arise from dreams. The prodigal's Daoist heart is due to this dream. When the dream is over, return the paper quilt to me." So, I wonder what kind of paper the so-called paper quilt is made of and how it can be so gentle. Moreover, it stirs up dreams and corrupts people's Daoist hearts. Gentlemen of erudition and elegance, can you teach me?

Inspiration and Associations from the Divine

— Wang Gongyu

Character Prediction is also called Character Decomposition. It is also called Character Breaking or Character Phrenology. It is a type of divination. A character is chosen at random, and its radicals and strokes are separated, combined, and cross-referenced, or it is associated by inspiration, to judge the good or bad luck of human affairs. The Zhìmíng Xīnfǎ (Direct Pointing to the Mind Method) says: When Tang Pei Jin Gong (Li Jing) was conquering Wu Yuanji, he dug up a stone with the inscription "The chicken is not fat, the wine is not ripe." The character predictor interpreted it as: "The chicken is not fat, there is no meat, so it is 己 (jǐ, the sixth Heavenly Stem)." "The wine is not ripe, there is no water, so it is 酉 (yǒu, the tenth Heavenly Stem)." "The defeat of the bandit will be on the jǐ-yǒu day." Indeed, it was. This is the beginning of character phrenology. Also, the History of the Sui Book: Classics and Books contains one volume of Essentials of Breaking Characters. The Yan Family Instructions say that this is the modern-day Character Decomposition. This is the origin of Character Breaking and Character Decomposition. By the Song Dynasty, there was Xie Shi, who was famous for Character Decomposition. Its origins have been long. However, the Character Prediction has not been deeply studied. As for those who set up stalls on the side of the road to earn a living, I have not seen them able to grasp the divine inspiration and associations. They are just talking nonsense. Recently, I was at a certain inn and listened to friends talking about strange events, which made me forget my fatigue. All the things they talked about were worthy of recording. So, I will first describe the section on Character Prediction. It said: There was a certain gentleman who set up a school in a certain county, which was quite famous. It shook the whole city. The magistrate of the county alone did not believe it and even harbored ill will towards him, wanting to expel him. However, in view of his usual interactions with the gentry of the county, who all praised him highly, he feared causing a backlash. So, he went to the gentleman's school in disguise to test his skills. He casually picked up a "人" (rén, person) character from the plate and said, "Please predict what kind of person I am." The gentleman did not hesitate and said, "You picked up the '人' character with one hand. Combining them, it becomes '大' (dà, big). You are an official." The magistrate was silent, left the fee as usual, and left. He then ordered his servant to go to the school in formal attire. The servant wrote the "人" character on his palm and asked the gentleman to predict what kind of person he was. The gentleman said, "Please don't be offended. You are a person under the hand of another person. You are a servant." The servant returned and told the magistrate. The magistrate was shocked by his accuracy. However, he still thought it was a coincidence. He then brought a prisoner from the prison, tidied him up, rode in a carriage to the school, and instructed him to verbally describe the "人" character. He asked the gentleman to predict what kind of person he was. The prisoner did as he was told and deliberately acted arrogantly, as if he were a wealthy old man. The gentleman still did not hesitate and said, "You are a prisoner. The '人' character in the mouth is a prison." The prisoner was discouraged. The magistrate, upon hearing this, believed him without a doubt. This is similar to the story of Qiao Gong Heqiao in our county. Qiao Gong knew our county and did not believe in ghosts and gods. Hearing that a certain spirit altar was very effective, he wanted to denounce it. Fearing that the local people would not agree, he dismissed everyone at night and personally drafted ten questions, all of which were impossible for people to answer. The next morning, he burned them in front of the altar and asked the spirit medium to answer them. Unexpectedly, the planchette moved on the sand, and in a moment, it answered all the questions one by one. At the end, it also attached a poem, revealing Qiao Gong's secrets. Qiao Gong was greatly shocked and convinced. He was terrified and at a loss. From then on, he worshipped the spirit altar more devoutly than others. To this day, the published version of Qiao Gong's Ten Questions and Answers is still circulating. The incident of the county magistrate's character prediction and the Qiao Gong's altar incident can truly be said to be "almost the same."

Special Prayers

— Yan Qian

There are many superstitious behaviors in our society. Special prayers are one of them. It is quite interesting to talk about. Please, readers of this newspaper, take a look at the following items.

(1) Using Destruction as Prayer: This refers to the act of destruction as a procedure for prayer. When villagers pay homage to the Buddhas in the Three Temples of Hangzhou, they often pass by the tomb of Su Xiaoxiao. They would pick up bricks and stones and throw them at the tomb pavilion, saying that this act is a way to pray for abundant silkworm harvests (meaning to profit from raising silkworms).

(2) Using Gambling as Prayer: This is probably the same group of people. When they pay homage at the tomb of Yue Fei, they often stroke the iron-cast breasts of Lady Qin Wang and say, "This year, our silkworm harvest will be 240%." (240% is a common expression for praying for silkworm harvests).

(3) Using Defilement as Prayer: Also this group of people. In addition to stroking the breasts of Lady Qin Wang, they would also pull down their pants and pour their "soul-returning soup" (urine) on the iron statues of Qin Hui and others, saying that it would also make the silkworm harvest good.

(4) Using Begging as Prayer: When a child suffers from malaria, their parents will try to please the Kitchen God. However, the method is somewhat different from the usual fasting for the Kitchen God. The tea used at the time was made by begging for tea leaves from seven households. Some also begged for rice or food from seven families. Others collected money from seven families to buy supplies for fasting for the Kitchen God.

(5) Using Theft as Prayer: A custom in the countryside of Wuxing County, Zhejiang: "After people are quiet in Mid-Autumn Festival, they compete to steal melons and rice. Those who get them are considered to have a sign of having a son." (See the Huzhou Prefecture Chronicle). Even thievery is transformed into prayer.

(6) Using Recitation as Prayer: On the walls of the urinal, there are often such red paper strips: "Heavenly Emperor, Earthly Emperor, my family has a crying baby at night. A kind person reads it once, and he will sleep soundly until dawn." This is another example of using recitation as prayer.

Travelogue of Southeast Asia (67)

— Ling Hua

On August 3rd, I went to Maymyo with Li Zhenzhong, Zhuang Haiquan, and Yang Zhen. Maymyo is located northeast of Mandalay, about 48 miles away. The four of us took a car for eight yuan. The road was high and lined with tall trees and small forests that blocked the sky. We often saw herds of cattle, but they did not have beautiful horns like those in Penang. Every mile had a stone marker indicating the mileage. Maymyo is the name of a very large hillside. After traveling more than 20 miles, we gradually went uphill, with extremely winding roads, similar to the car roads in Nanning, Guangxi. However, at the cliffs, there were stone walls, wooden posts, or iron wires to block them, to avoid driving dangers. This is the best method. Looking down at Mandalay, it was like looking from the sky. The clouds were six or seven hundred feet high. Just halfway there, the highest point of the mountain was 24 miles. There was a small parking spot with a flowing spring and stones. We washed our feet in it and immediately felt refreshed. This is an extremely cool place in Southeast Asia. The British Governor and the Chinese Consul often come here to escape the heat. Continuing forward, we went downhill. Along the way, there were various flowers of red, yellow, white, and purple, as well as fruit trees. I heard that Japanese people grow grapes here and can earn thousands of dollars each year. Gradually, we saw thatched huts, bamboo fences, grains, and vegetables. Burmese people farm here and live a very simple life. I heard that the spring water here is excellent, not only cool but also of high quality. We often saw clear streams flowing. Soon, we saw red houses hidden among the trees. We arrived at Maymyo City. This small market town is fresher than Yangon. However, there are only about one hundred Chinese people. There is a Chinese Association. When we knocked on the door, only an old man was guarding it. We couldn't communicate with him. There was a sign for the Da Ying School, but there were no students. They said it had disbanded. We stayed at the Liang Jinshan Villa. His brother-in-law, Mr. Yin, was guarding the house. Yin's father was Cantonese, and his mother was Burmese. He spoke English fluently. We asked about the Burmese King. He said that the Burmese King was captured in 1885 and died in India. We asked why the palace was so desolate. Many Japanese people came to build houses, but they have all collapsed now. We asked who the royal family members were. He said there were only three daughters. One married an Indian, and two married Burmese. How could they plan anything else? I asked the names of the royal daughters. He replied that he didn't know. We asked about the local products of northern Burma. He replied that Burma is a very rich place. Rubies come from Na Ga, yellow jade from Hukang, and green jade from Ma Geng, but I don't know the methods of mining them. Many Chinese people have become wealthy. This small market town has no English, Burmese, or Chinese newspapers. It is a rural market. There are Yunnanese inns and restaurants. Staying and eating two meals costs only one dollar per day. The dishes include meat and chicken, which can be considered cheap. Eating without staying costs the same price, half a dollar per meal, because there is no charge for lodging. The food is very delicious. Yunnan and Sichuan have the same taste, both are famous Chinese cuisines. During the day, we talked with Mr. Yin in a small building. Before we knew it, the window was open and the wind was cold. I couldn't stand it, so I asked to close the window. I even put on a long jacket. This was something I hadn't done in Southeast Asia for half a year. I suddenly felt cold. Singapore is below zero degrees. Going north past Mandalay, we had reached 23 degrees north latitude, in the temperate zone, on the same line as Shantou, Guangzhou, and Liuzhou, facing each other east and west, near the Yunnan border. Winter here may require cotton clothing. You don't need to shower with cold water usually. I had suffered from the heat for half a year. Now I had entered a cool place in Southeast Asia. I was indescribably happy.

Warmth in the Heart (304)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 15: Tears Fall on All Sides, Melancholy Red Affection; An Audience Overwhelmed, Lingering Green Intent

Looking at the fight, it was almost over. Everything visible in the room was in ruins. Even the quilts and pillows on the bed had been splashed with several basins of water. Little Sister, terrified, hid in the small room, trembling uncontrollably. Madam Yin then called a halt to the battle. As she left, she pointed at Lianxiang and said, "I'll spare you for today. When the master returns, he will settle the score with you." After saying this, she led the group of women she had brought and the chief of staff and vanguard, and left. After Madam Yin left, Lianxiang looked at the broken and ruined state of the room, and felt truly heartbroken. It was as if a major army had passed through, leaving the entire city in ruins. All the dressing tables in the room were broken, with shattered porcelain scattered all over the floor. They were all bought at great expense. Fortunately, the clothes in the chests and the jewelry in the cabinets were untouched. Lianxiang had already cried her eyes out. Little Sister, like a local official responsible for defending the area, returned to her old place after the enemy troops left. She tried her best to comfort Lianxiang. She said, "Crying is useless. We have to take care of the aftermath. We have to clean up the place. Don't throw away all the broken porcelain pieces. Leave them there for the master to see when he returns. They are proof for us for the rest of our lives. We are afraid he won't pay for the damaged items. If the old things are broken, we can replace them with new ones. But the bed is in such a mess. What are we going to do? How can we sleep tonight when it's so wet? Hurry up and open the chest and take out a clean set of bedding. I'll take the wet bedding to wash." At this point, Lianxiang had no choice but to endure and wait for the master to return and see what he would say. When the master returned, there was a big scene at home. The concubine also had no choice but to cry to the master about the grievances she had suffered that day. At this point, the Yin master almost flattened his head. Madam Yin's intention was, of course, to forbid the master from going to that side again. That kind of dirty goods should be kicked out. But if she was kicked out, how could the Yin master bear it? He had no choice but to move to another place. At home, he only said that the small villa had been canceled. In fact, he built a secret love nest elsewhere. Last time, the coachman Gengsheng was the one to blame. Gengsheng also knew that his job was gone, so he had no choice but to quit and find another place to work. The Yin master, fearing that the secret would be leaked, didn't take a carriage. Every day, he hired a rickshaw and sneaked to the secret love nest alone, thinking that he was foolproof. Who knew that he had this chief of staff who was also the captain of the detective team, the young master, who was ordered by his commander, Madam Yin, to keep an eye on his father. He was caught again. As Cuiyun was telling the story, someone came downstairs to hire her to sing. Zuo Shichen said, "Keep it simple. Finish it quickly."

Cotton Market Trends Upward

A Stable Situation May Be Difficult to Maintain. Over the past week, the cotton market has seen American cotton continue to rebound, shifting from a state of false weakness to stability. The difference from the low point is more than two taels, a significant change. It is noted that American cotton, due to repeated increases in production and persistently weak consumption, had been trending downward, reaching a ten-year low. Recently, thanks to the government's active publicity and stockpiling, the price has rebounded from one dime to one dime and two cents, and the upward momentum appears to be undiminished. This is because the price base is already low, and the upward trend is stronger. Recalling the period from March to April, the cooperative absorbed May and July futures, causing a rebound of nearly 300 points, but the result was a continued decline due to the relationship between production and consumption. The current situation is similar to the last time, with a force to pull up more than 200 points. However, after the third government estimate was released on October 8, news of favorable weather conditions spread, and the first heavy frost had passed. Reports indicated no significant damage. Furthermore, the sixth cotton ginning report showed 9,252,000 bales, similar to the bumper harvest figures of 1925. This suggests that the condition of the new cotton remains good. The next government estimate (November 8) may show a continuing increase, possibly reaching 14,500,000 bales. Whether the situation can keep pace with the supply is a crucial factor in the trend of the cotton market. Moreover, according to the World Textile Manufacturers Federation's report on global raw cotton consumption, the dominance of American cotton in the world cotton market is showing signs of wavering (the reporter will discuss this separately, so no more on that here). Looking back at the environment, the trend of the cotton market still lacks positive optimism. According to the reporter's assessment, the market is temporarily hovering in a stable position due to artificial maintenance by various parties, awaiting the next government estimate to determine its direction. Chinese cotton has also risen along with American cotton due to the lack of abundant production in various regions and the lack of a surge in arrivals. However, the continued invasion of foreign cotton, and the expected surge in new cotton arrivals in the future, may inevitably lead to another collapse. Furthermore, the pessimistic outlook for the yarn market is undoubtedly related. Therefore, based on the overall trend, the stable situation in the cotton market is likely only temporary.

Those covering their positions rushed in, and the market surged, with all months rising by 3.5 to 5 cents. In the afternoon, some profit-takers closed out their positions, causing a drop of 0.5 to 1 cent. The total transaction volume for the day was 96,400 dans. Public Tai sold 3,500 dans, Yi Kang 4,600 dans, Li Chang 4,100 dans, Yong Feng 3,800 dans, Rui Da 3,000 dans, and the rest 2-3,000 dans. Mei Ji bought 4,800 dans, Yu Da 6,300 dans, Tian Long 7,600 dans, Jin Feng 5,300 dans, Yu Chang 3,000 dans, and the rest 1-2-3,000 dans. The closing prices are recorded below:

Grains: Continuous Rain, Rice Market Gradually Rises

Zhabei. Yesterday, the amount of new rice arriving from various areas was not abundant, with only 20 to 30 boats. Sales for each were very smooth. The price for special grade new japonica rice opened at 14.7 yuan, with the market quickly seeing prices tighten by 2 jiao. The price was offered at 14.4 yuan, and transactions were still possible. The prices for medium and lower grades of rice increased by 1 jiao to 0.5 jiao because of the weather and public sentiment. But due to continuous rain, it was not easy to get more river boats. The arrival of Yangjian rice was sparse and sales were brisk, with prices rising by 3 jiao, opening high at 11.5 yuan. Buying interest was extremely high, and it would be difficult for the price of this rice to fall even if the weather cleared. The prices for Dujian rice from the port all rose by 2 jiao. The trend was not as strong as Yangxian rice because of a lack of inquiries from out-of-town merchants. Because the cost of superior quality rice was still very high, most merchants had to sell at a loss, so they asked for an increase of about 2 jiao. Special grade rice needed 10.05 to 10.06 yuan, and white rice had limited sales but was slightly firmer by about 1 jiao.

Hunan. Yesterday, more than 20 boats arrived. Sales on this street were not very extensive. The price of Changshu new japonica rice did not rise or fall but hovered around 14 yuan. Only a few retail buyers inquired about Sutong white japonica rice, and public sentiment was consequently flat. Prices were the same as the previous day. Sales of Yangxian rice were average, and sales of Dujian rice were slow. The above market prices did not rise or fall. Silver dollars were extremely scarce, and silver ingots were slightly more affordable. Each price lacked ups and downs.

Wheat Futures Rebound to Cover Shorts

After wheat futures opened yesterday morning and afternoon, public sentiment was good again. This was because the quoted price of foreign wheat had increased by 3, 4, or 5 jiao. Also, the standard delivery for October, a batch of goods, had been collected by factories. Therefore, the number of contracts would temporarily need to be reduced. Consequently, short sellers outside the industry were eager to cover their positions. For this reason, public sentiment for the forward months tightened, and trading for each month became more active. As a result, November rose 3 fen compared to the previous day, December rose 3 fen, January rose 5 fen, February rose 4 fen, and March rose 4 fen. Spot wheat prices were still good at the factories, and each grade of wheat increased by 7 to 8 fen. Shandong, Yaowan, Xinyangzhou, Gaoyou wheat, Jiangbei wheat, and Qingjiangpu wheat totaling more than 7,000 bags were purchased by Fufeng and Xinda.

Standard Soybean Futures Gradually Fall

Yesterday, the standard soybean market for each period was initially very flat and weak. Due to the lingering effects of the previous day, various parties continued to sell, so prices at the morning opening all fell by 4 or 5 fen. When the market opened in the afternoon, oil factory merchants started to buy, and the situation gradually stabilized as the gold market improved. Later, the Dalian telegram arrived in Shanghai with slightly firm news, so local merchants stopped selling, and each price rose slightly. As a result, the December contract was 4 taels 5 qian 8 fen, and the January contract was 5 qian 7 fen, both down 2 fen. The February contract was 4 taels 6 qian 1 fen, and the March contract was 6 qian 5 fen, both unchanged.

Sugar Market: Japanese Sugar Factory Opens Another 50,000 Bags

Market Allocations All Show Turnaround Increase

Yesterday, sugar market production area telegrams reported that the price of Cuban spot sugar was 1.46875, a decrease of 0.03125 compared to the previous telegram. New York sugar futures for December were 1.44, down 0.05. March of next year was 1.52, also down 0.06. May was 1.57, and September was 1.70, each down 0.07. The price of Java spot sugar was 8.125, and the price of November and December futures was 8 guilders, unchanged from before. The association's market allocation showed that Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse white sand had a special factory announcement of a price increase of 0.5 guilders, and public sentiment turned stronger. Sellers disappeared, and buyers still wanted to purchase, with the price reaching 7 taels 8 qian, and the highest price reaching 7 taels 9 qian. Although transactions were still scarce, the market was very firm. No. 20 medium white sand was 6 taels 8 qian, and No. 8 Dutch red was 6 taels 3 qian 5 fen. The market was relatively flat. The Japanese sugar market also turned upward. Minghua YRO mark was 7 taels 3 qian 5 fen, YT mark was 7 taels 6 qian 5 fen, and TK mark was 7 taels 7 qian 5 fen, each up 0.05. YP mark was 7 taels 8 qian 5 fen to 7 taels 9 qian, an increase of 0.1 qian. The market looked lively. The factory allocation of Minghua sugar opened at 30,000 bags, with a price of 5.8 Japanese gold yuan. Meiji sugar opened at 20,000 bags, with a price of 4.6 yuan. The delivery period was December and January of next year. Merchants were very eager to purchase and sold out completely, and there was a shortage of supply. The market was 0.1 yuan higher than the previous allocation, and the market was also strong. The trademarked Bingchang company sold spot No. 20 medium white sand for 3,012 bags at a price of 6 taels 8 qian yuan. Also, the company sold 2,000 bags of No. 8 Dutch red sugar arriving on the 2nd of next month at a price of 6 taels 3 qian 5 fen yuan. Demand was very strong, and the market looked very firm.

North-South Goods: Dried Peach Meat Market Stable

Recently, dried peach meat has arrived in succession. Market inventory is not high. According to letters, the prices in Tianjin and Hankou have not risen or fallen much. Sales here have been carried out by local merchants, as well as those from Jiahu, Changshu, and other regions. The trend is stable. Yesterday, the market price for Tianjin dried peach meat was 40 taels, and the next best was 38 taels. Yan dried peach meat was 34 to 35 taels.

Seafood: Squid Production Area Reports a Price Increase of 2 Yuan

According to inquiries, the production of squid in Hakodate and Tsushima has been affected by the lack of winter water in the ocean, and the arrival of goods is even more lacking than in the autumn. Therefore, the price in the production area has increased by 2 yuan. Although sales to Shanghai have not been active, merchants' costs are high, and the marked price has increased. Therefore, the price has not increased. Yesterday, the price for full Qing large sheet Hakodate autumn water squid was 44 taels 7 qian, uniform sheet unified goods were 43 taels 1 qian to 42 taels 6 qian, winter water Chaozhou goods were 42 taels 2 qian, oil-mixed sheet was 40 taels 3 qian, full oil sheet was 38 taels, and Yulin sheet was 35 taels 5 qian. A total of 139 pieces were sold. It is said that merchants still have more than 100 pieces remaining and are not selling them for the time being, waiting to see how the production area market changes before deciding what to do.

Silk and Tea: New York Factories Wire Transfer Prices Drastically Rise

Factories Still Say Silk Costs Are Insufficient, Negotiations Are Difficult

Yesterday, the silk market for foreign firms in Shanghai suddenly trended upward. According to inquiries, silk weaving factories in New York, seeing that the price of silk from Chinese and Japanese factories had fallen to the lowest level, took the opportunity to purchase spring raw materials. In addition, the exchange rate was tight, so the price of silk drastically rose. Yesterday, Jardine Matheson received a telegram from New York stating that Shanghai white factory silk had risen by 30 to 40 taels. Each factory still says silk costs are insufficient and is firmly continuing to raise prices before selling. A deal has yet to be reached.

Marseille Long Filature Prices Drastically Rise

Silk weaving factories actively purchase spring raw materials, prices up 2-3 francs

The Shanghai silk market for long filature silk has been trending firmer since silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang collectively agreed to suspend operations, and silk production has been decreasing daily. Yesterday, French firms received a telegram from Marseille stating that each silk weaving factory, seeing that Chinese and Japanese silk factories had suspended operations and the supply was gradually decreasing, began to actively purchase spring raw materials. The inventory was scarce, and market prices drastically rose. The current market price for superior grade Shanghai silk factory long filature is 85 francs per kilogram, an increase of 2-3 francs.

Gaozhuang Zhenmei Actively Sold in Europe

Yesterday, Zhenmei green tea from sources such as Tunxi continued to be purchased by companies such as Xiehe, Jardine Matheson, Yongxing, and Tianxiang, and transactions were not quiet. The top price for Tunxi drawn core goods was 200 taels. The top price for ordinary Zhenmei was 132 taels. Xiamu pearl tea was slightly in demand by companies such as Jardine Matheson and Duder, but the price they were willing to pay was extremely low. The Association still intended to increase or decrease the price of Gongxi green tea and Qimen black tea. Sales of medium and low grade goods remained sluggish.

Oil Market: White Tung Oil Sales Sluggish, Prices Plunge

The plunge in white tung oil prices in recent days has been unprecedented. Wholesale prices at foreign firms have fallen from 26 taels to 15 taels 6 qian, a difference of 30 taels compared to the 46 taels high in 1916. Even compared to the usual market price, it has fallen by more than half. Zhejiang tung oil has also fallen by 7 yuan and is only selling for 27 yuan. The reason for the price drop is purely due to sluggish foreign sales and a large stockpile of oil. Although cargo owners have repeatedly lowered prices, transactions are difficult to complete. With the autumn season of abundant production and stagnant foreign sales, there is a fear that after the major price drop, there will be further price declines.

Hardware: Autumn Rain Affects Hardware Loading

Yesterday, with the autumn rain drizzling, export merchants were all hesitant to load hardware, fearing that the hardware would be damaged by water stains and affect sales. As a result, the amount of hardware offered in the market was even more scarce. Although sales of various scrap iron items were usually brisk, sales were also unusually low yesterday. However, asking prices were higher due to the exchange rate situation. Even blue lead bars, which had been declining sharply, rose by 1 qian yesterday and were selling for 14 taels 4 qian 5 fen. Two-hundred-pound company iron rose by 2 qian 5 fen and was selling for 21 taels 7 qian 5 fen. It is said that canneries purchased 600-700 boxes yesterday, and the market supply is very scarce, so the outlook is good. The amount of tinplate offered was limited, but fortunately there were no market changes. There were still few buyers for nails, so it was still difficult for the market to recover.

Shaoxing Merchants Purchase 500 Dans of Spot Tin

The spot tin market has been sluggish for a long time, so there have not been any major transactions in the market for a long time. Earlier, Fuhao, Lengsheng, and other Shaoxing merchants purchased 500 bars of spot tin. Buying interest in the market was strong for a time. Although market prices did not improve, it felt much firmer than before.

Youth Corner

Escaped and Returned! To Calm the Nerves

— Chun

Because of Didi's earnest sincerity, I couldn't refuse, so on this silvery moonlit night, I rushed to Wusong.

Originally, I planned to see the sunrise. Wusong is a very suitable place to watch the sunrise. Someone had told us beforehand that when the morning sun rises, it will rise and fall more than ten times. The poetic situation is difficult to describe, so I was also happily moved by this painting of the morning sun. But when I woke up the next day, the strong sunlight had already sealed directly in from the glass window, and I couldn't help but feel disappointed. When I put on my clothes and looked out at the sea, the blood-red fireball was more than twenty feet above the sea. This caused our planned plan to fail. Later, Didi got up, and he told me that he had actually gotten up once at four o'clock when the east was still not white, but because the autumn wind was too strong, he was afraid I would get cold, so he didn't wake me up, and went back to sleep. Ah, Didi's deep affection is really enough to make me grateful.

However, playing is still playing. Our interest in playing is still so strong. After breakfast, after taking care of some miscellaneous matters, we discussed exploring the lighthouse.

The autumn wind was indeed strong, blowing head-on, making me gasp from time to time. The withering atmosphere of nature and the withered tones couldn't help but assault our thoughts, and we couldn't help but feel chilled and uneasy. Oh, how solemn and sad this late autumn is to people's hearts. We walked along the banks of the Huangpu River, the dust and sand flying fiercely. If a car or something like that passed by, we simply had to stop, turn sideways, and avoid it. We walked hand in hand, talking and laughing, and before we knew it, we were near the riverbank.

The sunlight reflected on the water, emitting a colorful luster. Looking ahead, one side is the Yangtze River, and one hundred is the East China Sea. In the middle, Chongming Island is vaguely revealed on the surface of the water.

Page 22

Looking across the Yangtze River, it's just a white wave and a seam separating the water and the sky. Towards the East China Sea, beyond Sanjia Water, it's also the same vast expanse of white. What punctuates it are only ships. In addition, it is the so-called interesting contrast between water and sky. We don't know whether it was intentional or melancholy that we looked into the distance for a while, and then followed the road to catch up with the road to the lighthouse.

The lighthouse is about thirty feet away from the shore. Large square stones made of mountain stones and concrete are piled up in a mess to form a road, connecting the lighthouse and the shore. We walked with big strides, sometimes shrugging our shoulders, but leisurely resting often, or looking into the distance, or talking and laughing, truly forgetting the so-called fatigue of life, and indulging in our heroic interest.

—To let the sea breeze blow on our chests, to completely blow away all the accumulated depression, so that our lungs are like being washed by a pure dew, this is so interesting. Ah, gentle sea breeze, blow so refreshingly, blow, let us bathe, bathe in your embrace.

I couldn't help but stretch out my hand, facing the slowly fanning sea breeze, and said to Didi,

—Yes, Didi also said sympathetically, this is really enough for people to enjoy. If it could be like this every day, it would be truly happy.

We walked forward unconsciously, and before long, the lighthouse was very clear. The lighthouse cannot be climbed. It is still more than a foot away from the embankment. We saw that the destination was about to arrive, naturally infinitely happy, but suddenly a voice came to warn us, making us stand still in shock.

—You go back quickly, the tide is rising very fiercely.

So we carefully identified where the voice came from. It turned out that the boatman on a small sampan parked next to the lighthouse was waving to warn us. In this way, we immediately paid attention to the tide. We saw that the upper reaches of the Yangtze River were surging down, much higher than before. But we still calmly observed the structure and form of the lighthouse, although we were already starting to worry in our hearts.

We came back almost running. However, it was impossible to come. We only ran five or six feet, and the stones in the lower part were already immersed in water, blocking the road. At this time, the waves surged, hitting the rocks, splashing waves, and the shoes were wet. At first, we were not afraid of getting wet and tried to cross over on the high stones, but in less than ten steps, almost all the stones in front were immersed in water, with only a few corners exposed, and the tidal waves were even more turbulent, making us unable to help but be afraid, so we stood still, on the stones a foot above the water surface. In fact, we really didn't understand the water flood. I also thought that the tide would recede soon, and would not rise any higher.

—Let's just stand here, I said. Since we can't leave now, then we can only wait for the tide to go back. I think it will be at most one or two hours. Anyway, it's good, let's just watch the tide here.

Athlete

—Photographed by Hua

At this time, I became optimistic instead. I didn't know that the danger was right in front of me.

—Really, we can sigh at the river today, Didi echoed.

But the tide was still rising, and the stones we were standing on were also unstable, having been washed by the waves several times. This gradually made me anxious, thinking about what would happen if it rose again, but at this time, I couldn't use words to comfort Didi.

—It's okay for the two of us to stand together. Even if the water rises again, it won't rise too high.

—Even if it's not good—, we will die together,

Didi said with a smile. I heard it, and my heart couldn't help but fluctuate, almost bursting into tears. Our hands couldn't help but grip each other more tightly.

Silence joined us. We seemed to be tacitly agreeing. I started to pay attention to the way back. Only a few stones exposed their corners above the water surface, and our surroundings were almost completely a world of water. We seemed to be floating, playing water games, like duckweed on the water, about to drift with the wind and waves.

The situation became tense little by little. We saw that the situation was not right, so we decided to get a boat to ferry us. We saw a ship passing by, so we shouted, but jokingly, the people on the ship saw us and thought we were just having fun, and did not lower any lifeboats. But our feet were about to be submerged in a marsh. So, seeing that we couldn't go down any further, we waved to the sampan parked next to the lighthouse, indicating that we wanted them to rescue us. Sure enough, they raised their sails and set off. We couldn't help but laugh wildly at each other, feeling the humor of this trip. When the boat approached, we jumped up, and the boatman was unusually kind. He saw our embarrassed situation, comforted us warmly, and asked,

—Where did you come from?

—From Wusong,

—Are you from the Marine Products School?

—No,

Ah... So you don't understand the tide. This is really dangerous. These days are the spring tides, and the tide rises a foot every half hour until you are submerged.

—Then at what time will it recede?

—At least five o'clock. Next time, if you don't know the tide, don't come, the boatman sincerely told us.

I turned back and smiled at Didi and said,

—Today is really a blessing in disguise.

Talking like this, the boat had landed. We gave them some money for wine and escaped ashore, our hearts still beating fast. We comforted each other and sat down on the ground to take off our shoes and socks to dry.

When we looked back at the road to the lighthouse, the water had formed a sheet. So we sighed for a while and gave our blessings.

Returning to Wusong, the sun had left its central position. We went to a restaurant and each bought a pound of wine.

—Let's make an exception and drink more. This is our calming wine.

Art World

Recent Spanish Literary Scene

— Ming

Best Book Club of the Month

The Death of Miro

Reading clubs, which have been very popular in England and the United States in recent years, have become popular in Spain. Madrid now also has such an organization, called the "Best Book Club of the Month" (Asociacion del Major Libro del Mes). However, unlike others, this reading club is not a disguised publishing organization, but an important group in the Spanish literary scene. Because its hosts are all modern Spanish literary giants, their selection and criticism are certainly enough to attract national attention, and contain serious implications. Therefore, if a writer's new work is selected, it is extremely beneficial to the author's own value and status. The important figures who host this reading club are as follows: Azorin, E. Diaz Canodo, Pedro Saing Rodriguez, Ramon Perezz de Ayak, Ricardo Baeza, Jose M. Salaverria, Rafael Altamia, and Gabrel Mirs. These are all important figures in the modern Spanish literary scene. Among them, Miro has recently passed away, and Miro's death has shocked and saddened the Spanish literary world.

Gasset, a Nationalist Writer

Longing for the Rebirth of the Spanish Nation

Gasset's (Jose Ortega J. Gasset) seventh volume of "The Spectator" (El Espeotador) has recently been published, and is one of the new books selected by this reading club. This is a collection of essays, and the nature of the topics is very uneven, from "Hegel and America" to "The South American Plains," all of which are discussed. Gasset is very knowledgeable about German philosophy. He said, "Hegel is the emperor of the thought world, the champion of scholars." However, he admitted that Hegel's shortcoming is that he cannot explain the history in formation. He does not understand the future of America. This is what Gasset discussed in his essay "Hegel and America." Moreover, Gasset said that Hegel's masterpiece "Philosophy of History" still has no translation in France and Spain, which is really a shame for the academic and publishing circles of these two countries. Therefore, he announced that he would soon translate this book into Spanish. In addition, in the essay "The Rise of Estdan" (Origen Deprortivo del Estado), he traced Spain's past military achievements, and as in his famous book "Invertebrate Spain" (España Invertebrada), he encouraged modern Spanish youth to use their activities for purposes that are more valuable than sports and games. Gasset is clearly a Spanish nationalist writer. He sees himself living in this lifeless era, and he feels extremely painful. He longs for the old courage and vitality of the Spanish people to flourish again. He found that Argentina and those Pampao (plains) are full of vitality, inhabited by the most enterprising people of all nations. These people all have strong primitive impulses, a fervent will to survive, and a magnificent human will. These all foreshadow that they will have a strong future and will achieve a lofty position in history.

Ramon Latre's Views

Spain is Not a Masculine Nation

Completely different in nature from Gasset's new book is Ramon Latre's interesting "Why Spaniards Have Not Achieved More" (Por que El Esqanol No Ha Llegado a Mas). His theory is very unique and very interesting. He said that because emigration and war have made the number of women in Spain much larger than the number of men, Spain is not a masculine nation (like the Anglo-Saxon nation), but a feminine nation. According to Latre, a masculine nation requires people of the same nation to be monarchs, while a feminine nation, like Spain, submits to the rule of foreigners. They Spain has never ruled other countries. Sicily and Naples were not conquered by the Spanish. The Aragon royal family went to the former because they got the consent of its people, and to the latter because they got the consent of its queen. Latre admits that Spaniards have one masculine trait: their resistance to Napoleon, and one feminine impulse: creating what is called "Spanish America" (Hispamerica, referring to the countries of South America). He denies that the creation of these "Spanish America" countries can indicate the Spanish people's conquest, estilo hsmbra (masculine style). He believes that this is only an expression of rich productivity, the so-called estilo hembra (feminine style). Moreover, he said that these countries were not conquered by the Spanish, but only ruled by the Spanish. Therefore, the subsequent separation from Spain is not a sign of Spain's decline. He cannot find any decline or decline in this Spanish race, but it is not ambitious enough and has limited vitality. But he believes that according to the methods he proposed, this shortcoming can be avoided.

From these words, we can know that Latre is a person who has special research on women. But unfortunately, he is a misogynist. His attitude towards women is the attitude of a misogynist, thin and contemptuous. Therefore, his book "Why Spain Has Not Achieved More" will certainly not be welcomed by the Spanish women's world, because Latre actually said honestly that physically, a woman is just a machine for creating human beings, and spiritually, she has nothing. The most enthusiastic thing in her life is to transform the exterior of her body into an exquisite chest of drawers. Her only history is the transformation in this chest of drawers, because she needs nothing but decoration. Women can eat bad things and live casually, but men, because of their mental and physical labor, need abundant food, excellent living conditions, and comfortable rest. Latre also said that Spanish mothers dote on their sons, making them all feminine. Women are the heads of households, but because they themselves are docile, they also pass on this docile habit to their descendants.

The Prevailing Period of Essays

The recent Spanish literary scene is a prevailing period of essays. Muncio's (Angel Dotor Y Muncio) new book is also a collection of essays, entitled "Mirador," which discusses modern Spanish articles and art, and can indeed shed light on this aspect. His chapter on Cervantes worship has a detailed discussion of Spanish essays involving the immortal "Don Qulxote." In addition, he has very precise criticisms of contemporary Spanish literary and artistic figures.

Castro's (Americo Castro) new book is also a collection of essays, called "Santa Teresa Y. Otors Ensayos," which is also a book about literature and history. Santa Teresa was a 16th-century Spanish female writer. According to Castro, although the great writers of the time, such as Cervantes, Lope de Vega, and Calderon, all had many readers, Santa Teresa's books were even more popular. Her works can be considered the most complete representative of the Castilian language in the 16th century. In addition, several essays in Castro's book discuss academic issues, about Spanish history or literature. Because of the author's broad knowledge, these essays are very meaningful.

The Spanish are now shouting for the revival of Spain, and are trying their best to connect this 20th-century revival with their traditions. Therefore, starting in the spring of this year, a very noteworthy new quarterly has been published in Madrid, Erudicion Ibero Ultramarina. The purpose of this review is to advocate the revival of Spain, while exploring Spain's past. The selectors are all famous Spanish scholars and writers. The three issues that have been published contain a total of more than 500 pages, and the content is very rich and the printing is exquisite. Each issue has about 20 pages of book reviews, and a column dedicated to Spanish art. In this column, in addition to articles, some less common Spanish paintings are inserted. The three issues have published a total of thirteen. For those who study Spanish culture, this magazine is indeed an indispensable good material.

Literary Anecdotes

Shaw's Complete Works and Preface

— Fu Lan

Shaw's complete works are printed in a very limited number, only one thousand and twenty-five copies. Each copy contains thirty volumes, costing thirty-one pounds and a half. In other words, the people who are currently ordering this book will pay a total of thirty-two thousand two hundred and eighty-seven pounds and a half, which is equivalent to five or six hundred thousand Chinese dollars. Its price cannot be said to be affordable. According to Shaw, who was recently interviewed by a newspaper reporter, "This book is only sold to fools and speculators." Perhaps Shaw has the courage to announce the names of those who ordered the books.

On the first volume of this book, there is an autobiographical preface by Shaw, which writes his own life story very faithfully, starting from his infancy, and then coming to London at the age of twenty to work as a bookkeeper for eighteen shillings a month, until the period when he wrote a novel that no publisher was willing to accept for publication.

Speaking of his unsociability, when he first came to the city, he also described his father.

Page 24

said,

"Unfortunately,... my father had a habit of only knowing how to close the doors and windows, and even prevented my mother from being properly invited. If there were no him,... if you invited him to dinner or a tea party, he would often be sober at the start, but would definitely leave drunk as mud... In the end, we became more and more estranged from society day by day."

"After I passed my childhood, I was never able to visit my relatives' homes. If my father and mother went out to dinner or attended appointments, their children were alone at home, and the fear in their hearts was worse than a house on fire. My mother was lucky to have her musical talent, which greatly helped her escape this predicament. And my father gradually moved from theory to practice in terms of temperance, because he had a spasm on the steps of my house one Sunday afternoon and fell to the ground, thus realizing that he must abstain from drinking, otherwise he would die."

"However, his reform was too late and could not save his social status, and I was even more at a loss as to how to socialize."

After Shaw's article was published, Dr. Cullier, the former president of the Baptist Church, recently gave a speech in Folkestone, saying that Shaw's description of his father's drinking was very faithful, but said, "If Shaw can make a valuable statement on this level, it is easy for us to forgive the issue of his politeness, but we would rather he not have a family profile. Why does he expose the facts of his father nakedly as a defense for his own shortcomings?"

Later, Shaw was informed by a reporter from a newspaper and replied to the reporter, "From his point of view, I certainly have no politeness. The good politeness in the ideal of a Baptist pastor is certainly something I cannot reach. I have described my father very faithfully. Anyone can see everything from me. I think it is better for me to tell my own story than for a Baptist to overstep his bounds."

Flowers by the Roadside

— Su

"In the morning, a girl from Yue Creek; in the evening, a concubine in the Wu Palace." This is a Chinese poem lamenting the fleeting fate of beautiful women. Although Xi Shi was discovered and brought into the palace of the King of Wu, countless other roadside flowers, scattered by the Yue Creek, remained unknown. This is a common lament of poets throughout the ages.

Here, I write about a roadside flower from the Parisian music scene. Her past is just like that of an unappreciated Yue girl by the Washing Silk Creek.

In the bright, southern European city of Paris, Parisians, lightly dressed, would happily stroll during early summer evenings, or take a short break in cafes filled with the haze of tobacco smoke and cheerful laughter.

The cafes, filled with whispers, whistling, and the clatter of cups and plates, featured a young singing voice every night. This singer, with her exotic appearance and charm, possessed a strong allure, making people forget about going home and lingering to listen.

This wandering songstress, no one knew where she lived. Only the young people who heard her sing would crazily wait for her every night at the cafe, some even following her from one cafe to another.

"I... I was born in Venice, the daughter of a boatman, growing up on the water. I have no surname."

She would always cheerfully answer those who asked her. An Italian girl, a boatman's daughter, growing up on the water—those who heard these self-descriptions would each imagine in their minds a warm summer night, the slowly flowing, mirror-like water, and the romantic tugging of bowstrings. It seemed as if she brought with her the fragrance and color held by that poetic southern land.

One day, she suddenly disappeared. Her beautiful voice was no longer heard in the cafes, nor was her bright smile seen again. The young patrons became depressed. Only the gloomy sound of cups and plates remained in the cafes. Everyone seemed to have lost their strength in the darkness. Everyone talked only about the sudden disappearance of the singer.

"That girl really left with a gentleman."

"A gentleman?"

"Yes, a very respectable gentleman, but not young, past middle age." They gossiped like this, but no one knew her true news.

"What happened to that Italian girl?"

Such questions were often asked, but accompanied by a collective sigh of disappointment, no one answered anymore. Months passed like this.

One day, everyone suddenly rejoiced, shouting as if they had found some treasure:

"Go to the Théâtre des Bouffes-Parisiens!"

"Go to the Théâtre des Bouffes-Parisiens!"

Shouting this phrase, like water, they rushed from the cafes to the Théâtre des Bouffes-Parisiens.

The Théâtre des Bouffes-Parisiens was a theater that reached its peak in the late eighteenth century, in Paris.

The Italian girl, whose figure had disappeared from the cafes since summer, suddenly appeared on this stage. Parisians, who had been lonely for so long, were, needless to say, happy to see her appear. Even other spectators, hearing her beautiful voice, could not help but marvel and praise her.

Yesterday, a boatman's daughter, a wandering songstress, had leaped to become a flower of the Parisian art scene. In one night, she made all of Paris remember her new stage name, "Prima Donna."

On her last night singing in the cafe, as she walked out, a respectable gentleman noticed her. This gentleman was the manager of the Théâtre des Bouffes-Parisiens. He had an exceptional passion for her beautiful voice. That very night, he took her to the theater.

From a wandering girl, she became a lucky flower on the Parisian stage, just like a roadside flower that is appreciated by someone, instantly increasing in value a hundredfold. Her name is Podi.

The Emotionless Greeks

— Su

Go-Tal, Victoria, was a famous dancer of the past, truly the leading figure in the dance world at the time. He was also very confident, once boasting,

"Europe has only three truly great figures: Frederick the Great of Prussia, Vitelli, and myself."

Therefore, he looked down on everyone. At that time, in the music world, "Gluck," who held a great influence and was revered as the god of music, was only seen by him as a music student. Once, "Go-Tal" needed a new score for his dance, but he came to "Gluck," whom he considered a mere student.

"Compose a Greek dance piece for me. This..."

"A Greek dance piece... Understood. What kind of piece do you want?"

"Well, but, Gluck, I want you to write a Chaconne (a type of ancient Spanish dance that originated in 1591, flourished in the 18th century, and is now obsolete). Can you do that? Hey..."

"A Chaconne," Gluck, annoyed by his arrogance, calmly replied, "A Chaconne? Didn't you say you wanted music for a Greek dance? Do you think the ancient Greeks knew about this Chaconne musical form? In reality, ancient Greece did not have such a thing."

Speaking these words coldly like a sword, Go-Tal, who considered himself one of the three great men of Europe, could only stammer:

"What? Didn't know? Didn't know the Chaconne? Hmph... Not knowing the Chaconne, those Greeks are truly an emotionless people."

Due to the failure of this negotiation, in Go-Tal's entire dancing career, he could not find a piece by Gluck. (Su)

Art World Submission Guidelines

(1) Manuscripts should be limited to news, reviews, and introductory articles about recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(3) Photographs should be limited to recent portraits of domestic and foreign artists and their works, as well as various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally. Do not write carelessly. Western text should be abbreviated as much as possible. If it is absolutely necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the translation.

Home
